     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wpdms_usgs_photo_point_reyes_national_seashore.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Wpdms_usgs_photo_point_reyes_national_seashore.jpg" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wpdms_usgs_photo_point_reyes_national_seashore.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Point Reyes National Seashore
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <b>
       Point Reyes National Seashore
      </b>
      is a 71,028-acre (287.44km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) park preserve located on the
      <a href="/wiki/Point_Reyes" title="Point Reyes">
       Point Reyes Peninsula
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
       Marin County, California
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA" title="USA">
       USA
      </a>
      . As a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_seashore" title="National seashore">
       national seashore
      </a>
      , it is maintained by the US
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_National_Park_Service" title="United States National Park Service">
       National Park Service
      </a>
      as an important nature preserve. Some existing agricultural uses are allowed to continue within the park.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clem_Miller" title="Clem Miller">
       Clem Miller
      </a>
      , a US
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congressman" title="Congressman">
       Congressman
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
       Marin County
      </a>
      wrote and introduced the bill for the establishment of Point Reyes National Seashore in 1962 to protect the peninsula from development which was proposed at the time for the slopes above Drake's Bay. All of the park's beaches were listed as the cleanest in the state in 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dirty_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-dirty-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Description">
       Description
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Point_Reyes_National_Seashore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Description">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The Point Reyes peninsula is a well defined area, geologically separated from the rest of Marin County and almost all of the continental United States by a
      <a href="/wiki/Rift_zone" title="Rift zone">
       rift zone
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/San_Andreas_Fault" title="San Andreas Fault">
       San Andreas Fault
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPS-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      about half of which is sunk below sea level and forms
      <a href="/wiki/Tomales_Bay" title="Tomales Bay">
       Tomales Bay
      </a>
      . The fact that the peninsula is on a different tectonic plate than the east shore of Tomales Bay produces a difference in soils and therefore to some extent a noticeable difference in vegetation.
     </p>
     <p>
      The small town of
      <a href="/wiki/Point_Reyes_Station,_California" title="Point Reyes Station, California">
       Point Reyes Station
      </a>
      , although not actually located on the peninsula, nevertheless provides most services to it, though some services are also available at
      <a href="/wiki/Inverness,_California" title="Inverness, California">
       Inverness
      </a>
      on the west shore of Tomales Bay. The even smaller town of Olema, about 3 miles (4.8km) south of Point Reyes Station, serves as the gateway to the Seashore and its visitor center, located on Bear Valley Road.
     </p>
     <p>
      The peninsula includes wild coastal beaches and headlands, estuaries, and uplands. Although parts of the Seashore are commercially farmed, and parts are under the jurisdiction of other conservation authorities, the National Park Service provides signage and seeks to manage visitor impact on the entire peninsula and virtually all of Tomales Bay. The Seashore also administers the parts of the Golden Gate National Recreation area, such as the Olema Valley, that are adjacent to the Seashore.
     </p>
     <p>
      The northernmost part of the peninsula is maintained as a reserve for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tule_Elk" title="Tule Elk">
       Tule Elk
      </a>
      , which are readily seen there. The preserve is also very rich in
      <a href="/wiki/Bird_of_prey" title="Bird of prey">
       raptors
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shorebirds" title="Shorebirds">
       shorebirds
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPS-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">

       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tupeelkpointreyes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tule_Elk" title="Tule Elk">
         Tule Elk
        </a>
        at
        <a href="/wiki/Tomales_Point" title="Tomales Point">
         Tomales Point
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Point_Reyes_Lighthouse" title="Point Reyes Lighthouse">
       Point Reyes Lighthouse
      </a>
      attracts
      <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">
       whale-watchers
      </a>
      looking for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gray_Whale" title="Gray Whale">
       Gray Whale
      </a>
      migrating south in mid-January and north in mid-March.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Point_Reyes_Lifeboat_Station" title="Point Reyes Lifeboat Station">
       Point Reyes Lifeboat Station
      </a>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">
       National Historic Landmark
      </a>
      . It is the last remaining example of a rail launched lifeboat station that was common on the Pacific coast.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nova_Albion" title="Nova Albion">
       Nova Albion
      </a>
      , Francis Drake's 1579 campsite;
      <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A3o_Rodrigues_Soromenho" title="Sebastio Rodrigues Soromenho">
       Sebastio Rodrigues Soromenho
      </a>
      's 1595 wreck; and fifteen associated Native American sites are included in the Drakes Bay Historic and Archaeological District
      <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">
       National Historic Landmark
      </a>
      . This encompasses 5,965 acres along the coast of Drakes Bay.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Kule_Loklo" title="Kule Loklo">
       Kule Loklo
      </a>
      , a recreated
      <a href="/wiki/Coast_Miwok" title="Coast Miwok">
       Coast Miwok
      </a>
      village, is a short walk from the visitor center.
     </p>
     <p>
      More than 30,000 acres (120km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) of the Point Reyes National Seashore are designated as the
      <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Burton_Wilderness" title="Phillip Burton Wilderness">
       Phillip Burton Wilderness
      </a>
      , named in honor of California Congressman
      <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Burton" title="Phillip Burton">
       Phillip Burton
      </a>
      , who wrote the legislation creating the
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_National_Recreation_Area" title="Golden Gate National Recreation Area">
       Golden Gate National Recreation Area
      </a>
      and was instrumental in helping to pass the
      <a href="/wiki/California_Wilderness_Act_of_1984" title="California Wilderness Act of 1984">
       California Wilderness Act of 1984
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The Point Reyes National Seashore attracts 2.5 million visitors annually. Hostelling International USA (part of
      <a href="/wiki/Hostelling_International" title="Hostelling International">
       Hostelling International
      </a>
      ) maintains a 45 bed
      <a href="/wiki/Hostel" title="Hostel">
       youth hostel
      </a>
      at the Seashore.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_Protected_Areas">
       Marine Protected Areas
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Point_Reyes_National_Seashore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Marine Protected Areas">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Point_Reyes_State_Marine_Reserve_%26_Point_Reyes_State_Marine_Conservation_Area" title="Point Reyes State Marine Reserve &amp; Point Reyes State Marine Conservation Area">
       Point Reyes State Marine Reserve &amp; Point Reyes State Marine Conservation Area
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Estero_de_Limantour_State_Marine_Reserve_%26_Drakes_Estero_State_Marine_Conservation_Area" title="Estero de Limantour State Marine Reserve &amp; Drakes Estero State Marine Conservation Area">
       Estero de Limantour State Marine Reserve &amp; Drakes Estero State Marine Conservation Area
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Duxbury_Reef_State_Marine_Conservation_Area" title="Duxbury Reef State Marine Conservation Area">
       Duxbury Reef State Marine Conservation Area
      </a>
      adjoin Point Reyes National Seashore. Like underwater parks, these marine protected areas help conserve ocean wildlife and marine ecosystems.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Drakes_Estero_oyster_farm_closure">
       Drakes Estero oyster farm closure
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Point_Reyes_National_Seashore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Drakes Estero oyster farm closure">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      A large shellfish farm raising Japanese (kumamoto) oysters,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crassostrea_gigas" title="Crassostrea gigas">
       Crassostrea gigas
      </a>
      , was located in
      <a href="/wiki/Drakes_Estero" title="Drakes Estero">
       Drakes Estero
      </a>
      until, under court order, it closed down at end of 2014. Court appeals to keep the operation in place were dropped in December, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The farm was purchased by the National Park Service in 1972, and the agency issued a permit to allow the previous owner to continue operations for 40 years. The business was sold to a new owner in 2004, the
      <a href="/wiki/Drakes_Bay_Oyster_Company" title="Drakes Bay Oyster Company">
       Drakes Bay Oyster Company
      </a>
      , who was informed by the NPS at the time of purchase that their permit to operate would not be renewed beyond the November 30, 2012 expiration date.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOI_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DOI-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A federal law enacted in 2009 authorized, but did not require,
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Interior" title="United States Secretary of the Interior">
       Interior Secretary
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Ken_Salazar" title="Ken Salazar">
       Ken Salazar
      </a>
      to renew the permit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CourthouseNews_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CourthouseNews-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The NPS and conservation groups viewed the farm as an inappropriate and environmentally-insensitive use of the estero, which was designated a "potential wilderness area" by Congress. The farm's supporters argued that it was not ecologically harmful and was important to the local economy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CourthouseNews_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CourthouseNews-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 29, 2012, Salazar announced that he would not renew the permit, citing the original intent of the Point Reyes Wilderness Act to designate the area as wilderness upon the removal of the oyster farm.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOI_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DOI-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Salazar visited the farm the previous week and later personally phoned the farm's owner to give him the news.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The oyster farm closure was challenged in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._District_Court" title="U.S. District Court">
       U.S. District Court
      </a>
      on January 25, 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The challenge was rejected by a federal court judge, who ruled that the law gave Salazar unfettered discretion to approve or deny a renewal of the permit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The California Coastal Commission voted on February 7, 2013 to unanimously approve cease and desist and restoration orders for violations of the California Coastal Act.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJ:_CC_ruling_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IJ:_CC_ruling-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">
       United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit
      </a>
      rejected an appeal of the district court's decision, ruling on Sept. 3, 2013 that the oyster farm's owner had not shown a likelihood of success on the merits because Salazar had acted within his discretion in denying the permit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFGateAppeal_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SFGateAppeal-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      An attempt to have the appeals court rehear the case was rejected on January 14, 2014 and a petition to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">
       United States Supreme Court
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was denied on June 30, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The oyster farm closed its on site retail operation on July 31, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, controversy continues over the condition of the estero sea floor and the ongoing off shore operations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another lawsuit challenging the closure itself was rejected in September 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PDrejected_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PDrejected-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hiking">
       Hiking
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Point_Reyes_National_Seashore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hiking">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG/300px-Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG/450px-Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG/600px-Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tule_elk_on_Tomales_Point_Trail.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Tule elk on
        <a href="/wiki/Tomales_Point" title="Tomales Point">
         Tomales Point
        </a>
        trail, further North (the Pacific Ocean is on the right).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Point Reyes has an excellent system of
      <a class="extiw" href="http://wikispot.org/?action=gotowikipage&amp;v=marin:Point_Reyes_National_Seashore" title="wikispot:marin:Point Reyes National Seashore">
       hiking trails
      </a>
      for dayhiking and backpacking. Bear Valley Trail is the most popular hike in the park. Taking off from the visitor's center, it travels mostly streamside through a shaded, fern-laden canyon, breaking out at Divide Meadow before heading gently downward to the coast, where it emerges at the spectacular ocean view at Arch Rock. A portion of Arch Rock collapsed on 21 March 2015, killing one person.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2046" data-file-width="2048" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg/220px-U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg/330px-U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg/440px-U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U-S-_National_Geodetic_Survey_marker_Mt-_Wittenberg_2014-03-25_00-56.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_National_Geodetic_Survey" title="US National Geodetic Survey">
         US National Geodetic Survey
        </a>
        marker at the peak of Mt. Wittenberg, the highest point in the park.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Three trails connecting from the west with the Bear Valley trail head upward toward Mt. Wittenberg, at 1,407 feet (429m), the highest point in the park.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_5-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPS-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Across the parking lot at the Visitor's Center is the Earthquake Trail which is a 0.6-mile (0.97km) loop that runs directly over the San Andreas Fault, deep underground, so that it is possible to stand straddling the fault line. The trail provides descriptions of the fault and the surrounding geology, and there is a fence that was pulled 18 feet (5.5m) apart during the 1906
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Earthquake" title="San Francisco Earthquake">
       San Francisco Earthquake
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the western end of the Point Reyes Peninsula is the historic Point Reyes Lighthouse, reached by descending 308 steps. Unlike many lighthouses, that were built high so the light could be seen by ships far out to sea, the Point Reyes lighthouse was built low to get the light below the fog that is so prevalent in the area. Nearby is the short Chimney Rock hike, which is noted for its spring wildflower displays.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_5-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPS-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As befitting a national seashore, Point Reyes offers several beach walks. Limantour Spit winds up on a narrow sandy beach, from which Drakes Beach can be glimpsed across
      <a href="/wiki/Drakes_Bay" title="Drakes Bay">
       Drakes Bay
      </a>
      . North Beach and South Beach are often windswept and wave-pounded. Ocean vistas from higher ground can be seen from the Tomales Point Trail and, to the south, from the Palomarin trailhead at the park's southern entrance outside the town of
      <a href="/wiki/Bolinas,_California" title="Bolinas, California">
       Bolinas
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      For
      <a href="/wiki/Backpacking_(wilderness)" title="Backpacking (wilderness)">
       backpackers
      </a>
      , Point Reyes has four hike-in campgrounds available by reservation.
     </p>
     <p>
      Point Reyes is a terminus of the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Discovery_Trail" title="American Discovery Trail">
       American Discovery Trail
      </a>
      which is the only transcontinental trail in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiscoveryTrail_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DiscoveryTrail-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">
       Flora
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Point_Reyes_National_Seashore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flora">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b6/Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG/300px-Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b6/Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG/450px-Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b6/Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG/600px-Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Point_Reyes_Fog.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Fog rolling in from the Pacific at Point Reyes National Seashore.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Point Reyes lies within the
      <a href="/wiki/California_interior_chaparral_and_woodlands" title="California interior chaparral and woodlands">
       California interior chaparral and woodlands
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">
       ecoregion
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In his book
      <i>
       The Natural History of the Point Reyes Peninsula
      </i>
      , Jules Evens identifies several plant communities. One of the most prominent is the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastal_Douglas-fir" title="Coastal Douglas-fir">
       Coastal Douglas-fir
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Pseudotsuga menziesii
      </i>
      ) forest, which includes
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coast_live_oak" title="Coast live oak">
       Coast live oak
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanoak" title="Tanoak">
       Tanoak
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_bay" title="California bay">
       California bay
      </a>
      and reaches across the southern half of Inverness Ridge toward
      <a href="/wiki/Bolinas_Lagoon" title="Bolinas Lagoon">
       Bolinas Lagoon
      </a>
      . Unlogged parts of this Douglas-fir forest contain trees over 300 years old and up to 6 feet (1.8m) in diameter. But despite these large, old trees, the forest may nevertheless be a result of European settlement. The
      <a href="/wiki/Coast_Miwok" title="Coast Miwok">
       Coast Miwok
      </a>
      people who once lived in the area set frequent fires to clear brush and increase game animal populations, and early explorers' accounts describe the hills as bare and grassy. But as the Native American settlements were replaced by European ones from the seventeenth century onward, the forests expanded as fire frequency decreased, resulting in the forests we see today.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fireHistory_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fireHistory-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Bishop_pine" title="Bishop pine">
       Bishop pine
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Pinus muricata
      </i>
      ) forest is found on slopes in the northern half of the park. Many of these trees growing in thick swaths came from seeds released after the 1995 Mt. Vision fire.
     </p>
     <p>
      Salt, brackish, and freshwater marshlands are found adjacent to
      <a href="/wiki/Drakes_Estero" title="Drakes Estero">
       Drakes Estero
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Abbotts_Lagoon" title="Abbotts Lagoon">
       Abbotts Lagoon
      </a>
      . The other communities identified by Evens are the coastal strand, dominated by European beach grass (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ammophila_arenaria" title="Ammophila arenaria">
        Ammophila arenaria
       </a>
      </i>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Carpobrotus_edulis" title="Carpobrotus edulis">
       ice plant
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Carprobrotus edulis
      </i>
      , also called
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_fig" title="Sea fig">
       sea fig
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hottentot_fig" title="Hottentot fig">
       Hottentot fig
      </a>
      ),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_rocket" title="Sea rocket">
       sea rocket
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Cakile maritima
      </i>
      ) and other species that thrive on the immediate coast;
      <a href="/wiki/California_coastal_prairie" title="California coastal prairie">
       northern coastal prairie
      </a>
      , found on a narrow strip just inland from the coastal strand that includes some native grasses; coastal rangeland, the area still grazed by the cattle from the peninsula's remaining working ranches;
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_coastal_scrub" title="Northern coastal scrub">
       northern coastal scrub
      </a>
      , dominated by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coyote_bush" title="Coyote bush">
       coyote bush
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Baccharis pilularis
      </i>
      ); and the intertidal and subtidal plant communities.
     </p>
     <p>
      Point Reyes is home to the only known population of the endangered Sonoma spineflower,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Chorizanthe_valida" title="Chorizanthe valida">
        Chorizanthe valida
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
